class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:World_Rally_Championship" title="Template:World Rally Championship"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:World_Rally_Championship" title="Template talk:World Rally Championship"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>World Rally Championship</b> (<b>WRC</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rallying</a> series organised by the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">FIA</a>, culminating with a champion driver, co-driver and manufacturer. The driver\'s world championship and manufacturer\'s world championship are separate championships, but based on the same point system. The series currently consists of 13 three-day events driven on surfaces ranging from gravel and tarmac to snow and ice. Each rally is split into 15\xe2\x80\x9325 <a href="/wiki/Special_stage_(rallying)" title="Special stage (rallying)">special stages</a> which are run against the clock on closed roads.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The WRC was formed from well-known and popular international rallies, most of which had previously been part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Rally_Championship" title="European Rally Championship">European Rally Championship</a> or the <a href="/wiki/International_Championship_for_Manufacturers" title="International Championship for Manufacturers">International Championship for Manufacturers</a>, and the series was first contested in <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Rally_Championship" title="1973 World Rally Championship">1973</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Car" title="World Rally Car">World Rally Car</a> is the current car specification in the series. It evolved from <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a> cars which replaced the banned <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> supercars. World Rally Cars are built on production 1.6-litre four-cylinder cars, but feature <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbochargers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-lag" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-lag">anti-lag</a> systems, <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel-drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Four-wheel-drive">four-wheel-drive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sequential_gearbox" class="mw-redirect" title="Sequential gearbox">sequential gearboxes</a>, aerodynamic parts and other enhancements bringing the price of a WRC car to around US$1 million (\xe2\x82\xac700,000 / \xc2\xa3500,000).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The WRC features three support championships, the <a href="/wiki/WRC_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="WRC Academy">Junior World Rally Championship</a> (JWRC, formerly the WRC Academy), the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-2" title="World Rally Championship-2">World Rally Championship-2</a> (WRC 2, formerly the Super 2000 World Rally Championship), and the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-3" title="World Rally Championship-3">World Rally Championship-3</a> (WRC-3, formerly the Production World Rally Championship) which are contested on the same events and stages as the WRC, but with different regulations. The WRC-2, WRC-3 and junior entrants race through the stages after the WRC drivers.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Coverage</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#TV"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">TV</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Radio"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Radio</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Internet_streaming"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Internet streaming</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Champions"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Champions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Event_wins"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Event wins</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Evolution_of_the_calendar"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Evolution of the calendar</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Other_classes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Other classes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Video_games"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Video games</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early">Early</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_4_(racing)" title="Group 4 (racing)">Group 4 (racing)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg/220px-Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg/330px-Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg/440px-Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="406" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancia-Stratos-HF-Group-4-%27.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group 4 <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Stratos_HF" class="mw-redirect" title="Lancia Stratos HF">Lancia Stratos HF</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The World Rally Championship was formed from well-known international rallies, nine of which were previously part of the <a href="/wiki/International_Championship_for_Manufacturers" title="International Championship for Manufacturers">International Championship for Manufacturers</a> (IMC), which was contested from 1970 to 1972. The <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Rally_Championship" title="1973 World Rally Championship">1973 World Rally Championship</a> was the inaugural season of the WRC and began with the <a href="/wiki/1973_Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="1973 Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo Rally</a> on January 19.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alpine-Renault" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine-Renault">Alpine-Renault</a> won the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_Constructors%27_Champions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Rally Championship Constructors&#39; Champions">manufacturer\'s world championship</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Alpine_A110" title="Alpine A110">Alpine A110</a>, after which <a href="/wiki/Lancia" title="Lancia">Lancia</a> took the title three years in a row with the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Dino_engine#65\xc2\xb0" title="Ferrari Dino engine">Ferrari V6</a>-powered <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Stratos_HF" class="mw-redirect" title="Lancia Stratos HF">Lancia Stratos HF</a>, the first car designed and manufactured specifically for rallying. The first <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_Drivers%27_Champions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Rally Championship Drivers&#39; Champions">drivers\' world championship</a> was not awarded until <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Rally_Championship" title="1979 World Rally Championship">1979</a>, although <a href="/wiki/1977_World_Rally_Championship" title="1977 World Rally Championship">1977</a> and <a href="/wiki/1978_World_Rally_Championship" title="1978 World Rally Championship">1978</a> seasons included an <i>FIA Cup for Drivers</i>, won by <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Munari" title="Sandro Munari">Sandro Munari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Markku_Al%C3%A9n" title="Markku Al\xc3\xa9n">Markku Al\xc3\xa9n</a> respectively. <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Waldeg%C3%A5rd" title="Bj\xc3\xb6rn Waldeg\xc3\xa5rd">Bj\xc3\xb6rn Waldeg\xc3\xa5rd</a> became the first official world champion, edging out Finland\'s <a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a> by one point.  <a href="/wiki/Fiat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> took the manufacturers\' title with the <a href="/wiki/Fiat_131_Abarth" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat 131 Abarth">Fiat 131 Abarth</a> in 1977, 1978 and <a href="/wiki/1980_World_Rally_Championship" title="1980 World Rally Championship">1980</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Europe" title="Ford of Europe">Ford</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_RS1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Escort RS1800">Escort RS1800</a> in 1979 and <a href="/wiki/Talbot" title="Talbot">Talbot</a> with its <a href="/wiki/Talbot_Sunbeam_Lotus" class="mw-redirect" title="Talbot Sunbeam Lotus">Sunbeam Lotus</a> in <a href="/wiki/1981_World_Rally_Championship" title="1981 World Rally Championship">1981</a>. Waldeg\xc3\xa5rd was followed by <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Walter_R%C3%B6hrl" title="Walter R\xc3\xb6hrl">Walter R\xc3\xb6hrl</a> and Finn <a href="/wiki/Ari_Vatanen" title="Ari Vatanen">Ari Vatanen</a> as drivers\' world champions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_B_era">Group B era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Group B era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg/220px-Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg/330px-Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg/440px-Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="1119" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Sport_Quattaro_S1_E2_in_2014_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group B <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro#Sport_Quattro_S1_E2" title="Audi Quattro">Audi Quattro S1</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The 1980s saw the <a href="/wiki/Rear-wheel-drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Rear-wheel-drive">rear-wheel-drive</a> <a href="/wiki/Group_2_(racing)" title="Group 2 (racing)">Group 2</a> and the more popular <a href="/wiki/Group_4_(racing)" title="Group 4 (racing)">Group 4</a> cars be replaced by more powerful <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel-drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Four-wheel-drive">four-wheel-drive</a> <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> cars. <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_du_Sport_Automobile" title="F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Internationale du Sport Automobile">FISA</a> legalized all-wheel-drive in 1979, but most manufacturers believed it was too complex to be successful. However, after <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> started entering Mikkola and the new four-wheel-drive <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Quattro</a> in rallies for testing purposes with immediate success, other manufacturers started their all-wheel-drive projects. Group B regulations were introduced in the <a href="/wiki/1982_World_Rally_Championship" title="1982 World Rally Championship">1982</a>, and with only a few restrictions allowed almost unlimited power. Audi took the constructors\' title in 1982 and <a href="/wiki/1984_World_Rally_Championship" title="1984 World Rally Championship">1984</a> and drivers\' title in <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Rally_Championship" title="1983 World Rally Championship">1983</a> (Mikkola) and 1984 (<a href="/wiki/Stig_Blomqvist" title="Stig Blomqvist">Stig Blomqvist</a>). Audi\'s <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> female driver <a href="/wiki/Mich%C3%A8le_Mouton" title="Mich\xc3\xa8le Mouton">Mich\xc3\xa8le Mouton</a> came close to winning the title in 1982, but had to settle for second place after <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> rival R\xc3\xb6hrl. <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Rally_Championship" title="1985 World Rally Championship">1985</a> title seemed set to go to Vatanen and his <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_205" title="Peugeot 205">Peugeot 205 T16</a> but a bad accident at the <a href="/wiki/Rally_Argentina" title="Rally Argentina">Rally Argentina</a> left him to watch compatriot and teammate <a href="/wiki/Timo_Salonen" title="Timo Salonen">Timo Salonen</a> take the title instead. Italian <a href="/wiki/Attilio_Bettega" title="Attilio Bettega">Attilio Bettega</a> had even a more severe crash with his <a href="/wiki/Lancia_037" class="mw-redirect" title="Lancia 037">Lancia 037</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_Corse" title="Tour de Corse">Tour de Corse</a> and died instantly.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_(27785248012).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_%2827785248012%29.jpg/220px-FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_%2827785248012%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_%2827785248012%29.jpg/330px-FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_%2827785248012%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_%2827785248012%29.jpg/440px-FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_%2827785248012%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FoS20162016_0624_153545AA_(27785248012).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group B <a href="/wiki/Ford_RS200" title="Ford RS200">Ford RS200</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg/220px-Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg/330px-Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg/440px-Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancia_Delta_S4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group B <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Delta_S4" title="Lancia Delta S4">Lancia Delta S4</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Rally_Championship" title="1986 World Rally Championship">1986</a> started with impressive performances by Finns <a href="/wiki/Henri_Toivonen" title="Henri Toivonen">Henri Toivonen</a> and Al\xc3\xa9n in Lancia\'s new turbo- and supercharged <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Delta_S4" title="Lancia Delta S4">Delta S4</a>, which could reportedly accelerate from 0\xe2\x80\x9360&#160;mph (96&#160;km/h) in 2.3&#160;seconds, on a gravel road.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> However, the season soon took a dramatic turn. At the Rally Portugal, three spectators were killed and over 30 injured after Joaquim Santos lost control of his <a href="/wiki/Ford_RS200" title="Ford RS200">Ford RS200</a>. At the Tour de Corse, championship favourite Toivonen and his co-driver <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Cresto" title="Sergio Cresto">Sergio Cresto</a> died in a fireball accident after plunging down a cliff. Only hours after the crash, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Balestre" title="Jean-Marie Balestre">Jean-Marie Balestre</a> and the FISA decided to freeze the development of the Group B cars and ban them from competing in 1987. More controversy followed when Peugeot\'s <a href="/wiki/Juha_Kankkunen" title="Juha Kankkunen">Juha Kankkunen</a> won the title after FIA annulled the results of the <a href="/wiki/San_Remo_Rally" class="mw-redirect" title="San Remo Rally">San Remo Rally</a>, taking the title from fellow Finn <a href="/wiki/Markku_Al%C3%A9n" title="Markku Al\xc3\xa9n">Markku Al\xc3\xa9n</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_A_era">Group A era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Group A era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_%281%29.jpg/220px-Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_%281%29.jpg/330px-Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_%281%29.jpg/440px-Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3109" data-file-height="2205" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancia_Delta_Integrale_-_Flickr_-_exfordy_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group A <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Delta_Group_A" title="Lancia Delta Group A">Lancia Delta HF Integrale</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lancia" title="Lancia">Lancia</a> is the manufacturer with the most wins in the WRC: 11 world Championship for Manufacturers, with 6 consecutives.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg/220px-Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg/330px-Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg/440px-Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Celica_GT-FOUR_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group A <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Celica_GT-Four" title="Toyota Celica GT-Four">Toyota Celica GT-Four ST205</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilson_Escort.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wilson_Escort.jpg/220px-Wilson_Escort.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wilson_Escort.jpg/330px-Wilson_Escort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Wilson_Escort.jpg/440px-Wilson_Escort.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1065" data-file-height="762" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilson_Escort.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group A <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_RS_Cosworth" title="Ford Escort RS Cosworth">Ford Escort RS Cosworth</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>As the planned <a href="/wiki/Group_S" class="mw-redirect" title="Group S">Group S</a> was also cancelled, <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a> regulations became the standard in the WRC until 1997. A separate Group A championship had been organized as part of the WRC already in 1986, with Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Eriksson" title="Kenneth Eriksson">Kenneth Eriksson</a> taking the title with a <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf_GTI_16V" class="mw-redirect" title="Volkswagen Golf GTI 16V">Volkswagen Golf GTI 16V</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Lancia was quickest in adapting to the new regulations and controlled the world rally scene with <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Delta_Group_A" title="Lancia Delta Group A">Lancia Delta HF</a>, winning the constructors\' title six years in a row from <a href="/wiki/1987_World_Rally_Championship" title="1987 World Rally Championship">1987</a> to <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Rally_Championship" title="1992 World Rally Championship">1992</a> and remains the most successful marque in the history of the WRC. Kankkunen and <a href="/wiki/Miki_Biasion" title="Miki Biasion">Miki Biasion</a> both took two drivers\' titles with the <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Delta_Group_A" title="Lancia Delta Group A">Lancia Delta HF</a>.\nThe 1990s then saw the <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a> manufacturers, <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subaru" title="Subaru">Subaru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Motors" title="Mitsubishi Motors">Mitsubishi</a>, become title favourites. Spain\'s <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz" title="Carlos Sainz">Carlos Sainz</a> driving for <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Team_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Toyota Team Europe">Toyota Team Europe</a> took the <a href="/wiki/1990_World_Rally_Championship" title="1990 World Rally Championship">1990</a> and 1992 titles with a <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Celica_GT-Four" title="Toyota Celica GT-Four">Toyota Celica GT-Four</a>. Kankkunen moved to Toyota for the 1993 season and won his record fourth title, with Toyota taking its first manufacturers\' crown. Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Didier_Auriol" title="Didier Auriol">Didier Auriol</a> brought the team further success in <a href="/wiki/1994_World_Rally_Championship" title="1994 World Rally Championship">1994</a>, and soon Subaru and Mitsubishi continued the success of the Japanese constructors. <a href="/wiki/Subaru" title="Subaru">Subaru</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scotsman</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_McRae" title="Colin McRae">Colin McRae</a> won the drivers\' world championship in <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Rally_Championship" title="1995 World Rally Championship">1995</a> and Subaru took the manufacturers\' title three years in a row. Finland\'s <a href="/wiki/Tommi_M%C3%A4kinen" title="Tommi M\xc3\xa4kinen">Tommi M\xc3\xa4kinen</a> driving a <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Lancer_Evolution" title="Mitsubishi Lancer Evolution">Mitsubishi Lancer Evolution</a> won the drivers\' championship four times in a row, from <a href="/wiki/1996_World_Rally_Championship" title="1996 World Rally Championship">1996</a> to <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Rally_Championship" title="1999 World Rally Championship">1999</a>. Mitsubishi also won the manufacturers\' title in <a href="/wiki/1998_World_Rally_Championship" title="1998 World Rally Championship">1998</a>. Another notable car was the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_RS_Cosworth" title="Ford Escort RS Cosworth">Ford Escort RS Cosworth</a>, which was specifically designed for rallying. It was the first production car to produce downforce both at front and rear.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Rally_Car_era">World Rally Car era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: World Rally Car era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Car" title="World Rally Car">World Rally Car</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ss1_5rb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ss1_5rb.jpg/220px-Ss1_5rb.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ss1_5rb.jpg/330px-Ss1_5rb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Ss1_5rb.jpg/440px-Ss1_5rb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ss1_5rb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Richard_Burns" title="Richard Burns">Richard Burns</a> in his <a href="/wiki/Subaru_Impreza_WRC" class="mw-redirect" title="Subaru Impreza WRC">Subaru Impreza WRC</a> after a <a href="/wiki/Rally_Finland" title="Rally Finland">Finnish stage</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg/220px-Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg/330px-Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg/440px-Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="856" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuoq_and_Latvala_-_2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peugeot_307_WRC" class="mw-redirect" title="Peugeot 307 WRC">Peugeot 307 WRC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_RS_WRC" title="Ford Focus RS WRC">Ford Focus RS WRC 07</a> on a road section during the <a href="/wiki/2008_Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="2008 Monte Carlo Rally">2008 Monte Carlo Rally</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>For the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Rally_Championship" title="1997 World Rally Championship">1997 World Rally Championship</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Car" title="World Rally Car">World Rally Car</a> regulations were introduced as an intended replacement for Group A (only successive works Mitsubishis still conforming to the latter formula; until they, too, <a href="/wiki/Homologation_(motorsport)" title="Homologation (motorsport)">homologated</a> a Lancer Evolution WRC from the 2001 San Remo Rally). After the success of M\xc3\xa4kinen and the Japanese manufacturers, France\'s Peugeot made a very successful return to the World Rally Championship. Finn <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Gr\xc3\xb6nholm">Marcus Gr\xc3\xb6nholm</a> took the drivers\' title in his first full year in the series and Peugeot won the manufacturers\' crown. England\'s <a href="/wiki/Richard_Burns" title="Richard Burns">Richard Burns</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Rally_Championship" title="2001 World Rally Championship">2001</a> title with a <a href="/wiki/Subaru_Impreza_WRC" class="mw-redirect" title="Subaru Impreza WRC">Subaru Impreza WRC</a>, but Gr\xc3\xb6nholm and Peugeot took back both titles in the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Rally_Championship" title="2002 World Rally Championship">2002</a>. <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Rally_Championship" title="2003 World Rally Championship">2003</a> saw <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Petter_Solberg" title="Petter Solberg">Petter Solberg</a> become drivers\' champion for Subaru and <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn" title="Citro\xc3\xabn">Citro\xc3\xabn</a> continue the success of the French manufacturers. Citro\xc3\xabn\'s <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Loeb" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien Loeb">S\xc3\xa9bastien Loeb</a> went on to control the following seasons with his <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_Xsara_WRC" class="mw-redirect" title="Citro\xc3\xabn Xsara WRC">Citro\xc3\xabn Xsara WRC</a>. Citro\xc3\xabn took the constructors\' title three times in a row and Loeb surpassed M\xc3\xa4kinen\'s record of four consecutive drivers\' titles, earning his ninth consecutive championship in 2012. Volkswagen Motorsport entered the championship in 2013 and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Ogier" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien Ogier">Sebastien Ogier</a> dominated the series with four consecutive titles. New World Rally Car rules were introduced for 2017 which generated faster and more aggressive cars.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg/220px-%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg/330px-%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg/440px-%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2728" data-file-height="1636" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C5%A0koda_Motorsport_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\xc5\xa0koda preparing their cars a day before the <i><a href="/wiki/Shakedown_(testing)" title="Shakedown (testing)">shakedown</a></i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Each season normally consists of 13 rallies driven on surfaces ranging from gravel and tarmac to snow and ice. Points from these events are calculated towards the drivers\' and manufacturers\' world championships. The driver\'s championship and manufacturer\'s championship are separate championships, but based on the same point system. This means, for example, that <a href="/wiki/Petter_Solberg" title="Petter Solberg">Petter Solberg</a> driving for <a href="/wiki/Subaru_World_Rally_Team" title="Subaru World Rally Team">Subaru</a> can win the driver\'s championship but <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_World_Rally_Team" title="Citro\xc3\xabn World Rally Team">Citro\xc3\xabn</a> can win the manufacturer\'s championship, which is what happened in <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Rally_Championship" title="2003 World Rally Championship">2003</a>, and again in <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Rally_Championship" title="2006 World Rally Championship">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Rally_Championship" title="2007 World Rally Championship">2007</a> when <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Loeb" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien Loeb">S\xc3\xa9bastien Loeb</a> took his third and fourth WRC titles but <a href="/wiki/Ford_World_Rally_Team" title="Ford World Rally Team">Ford</a> won the manufacturer\'s championship.\n</p><p>Under the current points system, points are awarded at the end of each rally to the top ten overall finishers in the World Rally Championship standings, as well as to the top ten finishers within the <a href="/wiki/Super_2000_World_Rally_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Super 2000 World Rally Championship">Super 2000 and Production Car</a> (also known as WRC 2), <a href="/wiki/Production_World_Rally_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Production World Rally Championship">two-wheel drive</a> (also known as WRC 3) and <a href="/wiki/Junior_World_Rally_Championship" title="Junior World Rally Championship">Junior World Rally Championships</a>. All categories use the following points structure:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:85%; text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Position\n</th>\n<td style="background:#ffffbf;">&#160;<b>1st</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfdfdf;">&#160;<b>2nd</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ffdf9f;">&#160;<b>3rd</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>4th</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>5th</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>6th</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>7th</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>8th</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>9th</b>&#160;\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">&#160;<b>10th</b>&#160;\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Points\n</th>\n<td style="background:#ffffbf;">25\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfdfdf;">18\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ffdf9f;">15\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">12\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">10\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">8\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">6\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">4\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">2\n</td>\n<td style="background:#dfffdf;">1\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Despite how many drivers are in one team, constructors may only nominate two drivers to score points for the team as well as scoring for themselves. As only nominated drivers are counted while awarding points, competitors placed further down the final standings than tenth overall (if preceded by <a href="/wiki/Privateer_(motorsport)" title="Privateer (motorsport)">privateer</a> drivers) can score them.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg/220px-Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg/330px-Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg/440px-Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gr%C3%B6nholm_vs._Loeb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A stadium-based <a href="/wiki/Super_special_stage" class="mw-redirect" title="Super special stage">super special stage</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rally_Argentina" title="Rally Argentina">Argentina</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the current era, each rally usually consists of between fifteen and thirty <a href="/wiki/Special_stage_(rallying)" title="Special stage (rallying)">special stages</a> of distances ranging from under 2&#160;km (1.2&#160;mi) (known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_special_stages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Super special stages (page does not exist)">super special stages</a>) to over 50 kilometres (31&#160;mi). These competitive stages are driven on closed roads which are linked by non-competitive road sections\xe2\x80\x94open roads on which all road laws of that country must be adhered to. On average a day consists of a total of 400 kilometres (250&#160;mi) of driving.<sup id="cite_ref-rallyireland_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rallyireland-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> A WRC event begins with reconnaissance (<i>recce</i>) on Tuesday and Wednesday, allowing crews to drive through the stages and create or update their <a href="/wiki/Pace_notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Pace notes">pace notes</a>. On Thursday, teams can run through the <a href="/wiki/Shakedown_(testing)" title="Shakedown (testing)">shakedown</a> stage to practice and test their set-ups. The competition typically begins on Friday and ends on Sunday, though some rallies\xe2\x80\x94most notably the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo Rally</a>\xe2\x80\x94may be run over four or five days. Cars start the stages at two-minute intervals in clear weather, or three-minute intervals if it is decided that visibility may be a problem for competitors. Each day, or <i><a href="/wiki/Leg_(rallying)" title="Leg (rallying)">leg</a></i>, has a few designated service parks between the stages, where the teams can \xe2\x80\x93 within strict time limits \xe2\x80\x93 perform maintenance and repairs on their cars. The service park also allows spectators and the media to get close to the teams and their cars and drivers. Between the days, after a 45-minute end of day service, cars are locked away in <a href="/wiki/Parc_ferm%C3%A9" title="Parc ferm\xc3\xa9">parc ferm\xc3\xa9</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rallyireland_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rallyireland-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> a quarantine environment where teams are not permitted to access or work on their cars.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_Stage">Power Stage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Power Stage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>First introduced in <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Rally_Championship" title="2011 World Rally Championship">2011</a>, the "power stage" is the final stage of the rally. Additional World Championship points are available to the three (until 2016) fastest drivers through the stage (regardless of where they actually finished in the rally), with the fastest team receiving three points, the second-fastest receiving two points, and the third-fastest receiving one point. In <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Rally_Championship" title="2017 World Rally Championship">2017</a> the scoring system was amended so the five fastest drivers through the stage were awarded points from five for first to one for fifth. For special stages, timing will be to the tenth of a second. For the "Power Stage", timing will be to the thousandth of a second. <sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Top Winners</b> <i>(Updated after <a href="/wiki/2018_Rally_Turkey" title="2018 Rally Turkey">2018 Rally Turkey</a>)</i>\n</p>\n<table title="Ott T\xc3\xa4nak">Ott T\xc3\xa4nak</a></td>\n<td>6\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rally_2">Rally 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rally 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Originally known as "SuperRally," Rally 2 is a set of regulations that allow a driver who retires from an event to re-enter the next day at the cost of a seven-minute time penalty for each missed stage (ten-minute penalty if only one stage is missed). This allows drivers who retire from an event to continue on and compete for World Championship points; however, if they retire on the final leg of a rally, re-entering is not possible. Similarly, the use of Rally 2 regulations is at the discretion of event organisers.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cars">Cars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_R" title="Group R">Group R</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Car" title="World Rally Car">World Rally Car</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Group_N" title="Group N">Group N</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg/220px-Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg/330px-Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg/440px-Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andy_Priaulx_-_2007_Race_of_Champions_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Andy_Priaulx" title="Andy Priaulx">Andy Priaulx</a> driving a <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_RS_WRC" title="Ford Focus RS WRC">Ford Focus RS WRC 07</a> at the 2007 Race of Champions.</div></div></div>\n<p>The current cars with 1.6&#160;L <a href="/wiki/Fuel_injection#Direct_injection" title="Fuel injection">direct injection</a> <a href="/wiki/Turbo_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Turbo engine">turbo engines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> are built to <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Car" title="World Rally Car">World Rally Car</a> regulations for racing across tarmac, gravel and snow. The power output is limited to around 380&#160;bhp (225&#160;kW). Current cars in the championship include the <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C3_WRC" title="Citro\xc3\xabn C3 WRC">Citro\xc3\xabn C3 WRC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta_WRC" title="Ford Fiesta WRC">Ford Fiesta WRC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_WRC" title="Toyota Yaris WRC">Toyota Yaris WRC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_i20_Coupe_WRC" title="Hyundai i20 Coupe WRC">Hyundai i20 Coupe WRC</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Polo_R_WRC" title="Volkswagen Polo R WRC">Volkswagen Polo R WRC</a> ended its run with the close of the 2016 season.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The WRC was formerly held for <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a> and <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> rallycars. However, due to the increasing power, lack of reliability and a series of fatal accidents during the <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Rally_Championship" title="1986 World Rally Championship">1986</a> rally, <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> was permanently banned. Later, in <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Rally_Championship" title="1997 World Rally Championship">1997</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a> cars evolved into the WRC car spec, to ease the development of new cars and bring new makes to the competition. In <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Rally_Championship" title="2011 World Rally Championship">2011</a>, new rules were introduced to encourage more manufacturers (and privateers) to take part, because the recent economic downturn had prompted several manufacturers to leave the championship.\n</p><p>Cars in the <a href="/wiki/Production_Car_World_Rally_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Production Car World Rally Championship">Production Car World Rally Championship</a> are limited to production-based cars <a href="/wiki/Homologated" class="mw-redirect" title="Homologated">homologated</a> under <a href="/wiki/Group_N" title="Group N">Group N</a> rules. Cars in the <a href="/wiki/Super_2000_World_Rally_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Super 2000 World Rally Championship">Super 2000 World Rally Championship</a> are homologated under <a href="/wiki/Super_2000" title="Super 2000">Super 2000</a> rules. Most cars in the <a href="/wiki/Junior_World_Rally_Championship" title="Junior World Rally Championship">Junior World Rally Championship</a> are homologated under <a href="/wiki/Super_1600" title="Super 1600">Super 1600</a> rules, but Group N and selected Group A cars can also contest the series.\n</p><p>Starting in 2013, a new category of rally cars known as <a href="/wiki/Group_R" title="Group R">Group R</a> were introduced as a replacement to the Group A and Group N rally categories, with cars classified under one of six categories based on their engine capacity and type, wheelbase, and drivetrain. As a result, no cars will be homologated under Group A and Group N regulations and instead will be reclassified under Group R. Parallel to this, the Super 2000 and Production Car World Championships were restructured; Super 2000 and Group N cars were merged into a single championship known as <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-2" title="World Rally Championship-2">World Rally Championship-2</a> alongside R4 and R5 cars, whilst the Production Car World Championship was completely reimagined as the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-3" title="World Rally Championship-3">World Rally Championship-3</a> for two-wheel drive cars complying with R1, R2 and R3 regulations.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams_and_drivers">Teams and drivers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Teams and drivers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg/220px-Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg/330px-Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg/440px-Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm_Bunnings_Jumps.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ford_World_Rally_Team" title="Ford World Rally Team">Ford</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Gr\xc3\xb6nholm">Marcus Gr\xc3\xb6nholm</a> at the Bunnings Jumps of the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Rally_Championship" title="2006 World Rally Championship">2006</a> <a href="/wiki/Rally_Australia" title="Rally Australia">Rally Australia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mg2_peugeot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Mg2_peugeot.jpg/220px-Mg2_peugeot.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Mg2_peugeot.jpg/330px-Mg2_peugeot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Mg2_peugeot.jpg/440px-Mg2_peugeot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mg2_peugeot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Gr\xc3\xb6nholm">Marcus Gr\xc3\xb6nholm</a> at the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Rally_Finland" title="Rally Finland">Rally Finland</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>21 different manufacturers have won a World Rally Championship event,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and a further 11 have finished on the podium.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Suzuki_World_Rally_Team" title="Suzuki World Rally Team">Suzuki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subaru_World_Rally_Team" title="Subaru World Rally Team">Subaru</a> pulled out of the WRC at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Rally_Championship" title="2008 World Rally Championship">2008 championship</a>, both citing the economic downturn then affecting the automotive industry for their withdrawal.  <a href="/wiki/Mini" title="Mini">Mini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford">Ford</a> both pulled out of the WRC at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Rally_Championship" title="2012 World Rally Championship">2012 championship</a>, due to a similar economic downturn affecting the European market, although Ford continued to give technical support to <a href="/wiki/M-Sport" title="M-Sport">M-Sport</a>.\n</p><p>A typical WRC team will consist of about 40 people on the events, with a further 60\xe2\x80\x93100 at the team base.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Manufacturers and manufacturer-backed teams usually have two or three drivers participating in each rally who are eligible to score points. The total number of crews (driver and his <a href="/wiki/Co-driver" title="Co-driver">co-driver</a>) in the rallies varied from 47 (<a href="/wiki/2007_Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="2007 Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_Rally_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Rally Mexico">Mexico</a>) to 108 (<a href="/wiki/2007_Rally_GB" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Rally GB">Great Britain</a>) during the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Rally_Championship" title="2007 World Rally Championship">2007</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_World_Rally_Team" title="Ford World Rally Team">Ford World Rally Team</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mini_WRC_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Mini WRC Team">Mini WRC Team</a> both announced their departure from the World Rally Championships for the 2013 season. <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Motorsport" title="Volkswagen Motorsport">Volkswagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_World_Rally_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyundai World Rally Team">Hyundai</a> made their return to the championship in 2013 and 2014, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> announced it will return to the World Rally Championships for the 2017 season <sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> with its Toyota Gazoo Racing team and its <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Yaris_WRC" title="Toyota Yaris WRC">Toyota Yaris WRC</a> car. Also <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn" title="Citro\xc3\xabn">Citro\xc3\xabn</a> will return to the sport in 2017 with a fully factory-supported team after competing part-time in 2016 to focus on the development of their 2017-generation brand-new car based on the <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C3" title="Citro\xc3\xabn C3">Citro\xc3\xabn C3</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rallies">Rallies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rallies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><i>See <a href="/wiki/2018_World_Rally_Championship#Calendar" title="2018 World Rally Championship">2018 WRC</a></i> for current season\'s rallies and <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_rallies" title="List of World Rally Championship rallies">List of WRC rallies</a></i> for a list of all rallies. \n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship#Evolution_of_the_calendar" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship \xc2\xa7&#160;Evolution of the calendar</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coverage">Coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TV">TV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: TV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_broadcasters" title="List of World Rally Championship broadcasters">List of World Rally Championship broadcasters</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg/220px-Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg/330px-Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg/440px-Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jari-Matti_Latvala_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A cameraman at a <a href="/wiki/Hairpin_turn" title="Hairpin turn">hairpin turn</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rallye_Deutschland" title="2007 Rallye Deutschland">2007 Rallye Deutschland</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Promoter GmbH owns the commercial rights to the championship and through WRC TV produces daily updates from each event after the day\'s stages have finished and the TV coverage has been processed. These daily highlight programs are 30 minutes in duration and cover in depth the day\'s stages, with in-car footage as well as driver interviews. Before the rally there is also a magazine-style preview programme that normally incorporates special driver, technical and team features as well as providing an overview of the upcoming rally\'s route. There is also a post-event review program, which lasts approximately an hour, that summarises the rally and the big events that took place during the event.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg/220px-Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg/330px-Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg/440px-Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2396" data-file-height="1876" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mitsubishi_WRT_-_2005_Cyprus_Rally.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mitsubishi service park at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_Rally" title="Cyprus Rally">Cyprus Rally</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>This is then shown in more than 150 markets in multiple languages. The make up and format for these programmes can change from country to country depending on the local broadcaster but all use WRC TV.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, coverage of the 2017 season is split between four broadcasters. <a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" title="Channel 5 (UK)">Channel 5</a> broadcasts the post-event review, while the preview programme is screened on its Spike network. <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> has rights to live stages and daily highlights, <a href="/wiki/Motors_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Motors TV">Motors TV</a> has highlights rights and Welsh language channel S4C also covers the championship in its Ralio programme.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, the cumulative worldwide TV audience for WRC TV\'s programmes was more than 700 million. The programming was available in over 150 markets and more than 12,000 hours were screened globally.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Live radio coverage was provided in English by WRC Live via the Internet, featuring end of stage reports direct from the drivers and teams plus service park news. They also produced podcasts. It also featured contemporary music during breaks in rally coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Currently the radio plays the sound of WRC+ All Live.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_streaming">Internet streaming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Internet streaming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/WRC%2B" title="WRC+">WRC+</a></div>\n<p>Coverage is provided by WRC Promoter GmbH via video on demand at its <a href="/wiki/WRC%2B" title="WRC+">WRC+</a> website featuring live special stages, highlights, timing, onboard footage and live map tracking.<sup id="cite_ref-plus_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plus-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2018, <a href="/wiki/WRC%2B" title="WRC+">WRC+</a> All Live was introduced, producing live coverage from all the stages during rally event.<sup id="cite_ref-plus_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plus-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions">Champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Renault_Clio_S1600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Super_1600" title="Super 1600">Super 1600</a> class <a href="/wiki/Renault_Clio" title="Renault Clio">Renault Clio</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grande_Punto_S2000_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grande_Punto_S2000_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fiat_Grande_Punto" title="Fiat Grande Punto">Fiat Grande Punto</a> Abarth S2000.</div></div></div>\n<p>The World Rally Championship also features support championships called the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-2" title="World Rally Championship-2">World Rally Championship-2</a> (previously known as S-WRC), the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-3" title="World Rally Championship-3">World Rally Championship-3</a> (previously known as P-WRC) and the <a href="/wiki/Junior_World_Rally_Championship" title="Junior World Rally Championship">Junior World Rally Championship</a> (J-WRC). These championships are contested on the same events and stages as the WRC.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Super_2000_World_Rally_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Super 2000 World Rally Championship">Super 2000 World Rally Championship</a> (S-WRC) was started in 2010. Within the Super 2000 category are competitions for drivers (known as the S-WRC) and another for teams (the World Rally Championship Cup). The cars in the championship are under the <a href="/wiki/Super_2000" title="Super 2000">Super 2000</a> rules.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> From 2013, <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-2" title="World Rally Championship-2">WRC-2</a> replaced S-WRC and including cars with four-wheel drive (R5, R4 and S2000).<sup id="cite_ref-WRC23_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRC23-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WRC2-3_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRC2-3-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Production_car_World_Rally_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Production car World Rally Championship">Production car World Rally Championship</a> (P-WRC) began in 2002, replacing the FIA <a href="/wiki/Group_N" title="Group N">Group N</a> Cup which had been contested from 1987. Cars in the championship are production-based and homologated under Group N rules.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> From 2013, the Production WRC was renamed <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship-3" title="World Rally Championship-3">WRC-3</a> including <a href="/wiki/Group_R" title="Group R">Group R</a> cars with two-wheel drive (R3, R2 and R1).<sup id="cite_ref-WRC23_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRC23-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WRC2-3_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRC2-3-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Junior_World_Rally_Championship" title="Junior World Rally Championship">Junior World Rally Championship</a> (J-WRC) was started in 2001, and can be contested with <a href="/wiki/Super_1600" title="Super 1600">Super 1600</a>, Group N and selected <a href="/wiki/Group_A" title="Group A">Group A</a> cars. Drivers in the championship have to be 28 years or younger. There is no age limit for <a href="/wiki/Co-driver" title="Co-driver">co-drivers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship_Ladies_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="World Rally Championship Ladies Cup (page does not exist)">World Rally Championship Ladies Cup</a> ran from 1990 to 1995 and could be won by any class of car. <a href="/wiki/Louise_Aitken-Walker" title="Louise Aitken-Walker">Louise Aitken-Walker</a> was the first winner.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Class</th>\n<th>WRC</th>\n<th>WRC-2</th>\n<th>WRC-3</th>\n<th>JWRC\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: black; font-weight: bold; vertical-align: middle; text-align: left;" class="table-rh">Group</td>\n<td>WRC</td>\n<td>S2000, N4, R5</td>\n<td>R1, R2, R3</td>\n<td>R3T, S1600\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: black; font-weight: bold; vertical-align: middle; text-align: left;" class="table-rh">Drivetrain</td>\n<td colspan="2">Four-wheel drive</td>\n<td colspan="2">Two-wheel drive\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: black; font-weight: bold; vertical-align: middle; text-align: left;" class="table-rh">Minimum weight (kg)</td>\n<td>1200</td>\n<td>1230</td>\n<td>980</td>\n<td>1150\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: black; font-weight: bold; vertical-align: middle; text-align: left;" class="table-rh">Typical power (hp)</td>\n<td>300</td>\n<td>280</td>\n<td>210</td>\n<td>163\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: black; font-weight: bold; vertical-align: middle; text-align: left;" class="table-rh">Torque (N\xe2\x8b\x85m)</td>\n<td>450</td>\n<td>360</td>\n<td>350</td>\n<td>182\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_video_games" title="List of World Rally Championship video games">List of World Rally Championship video games</a></div>\n<p>There have been many <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a> based on the World Rally Championship, and due to lack of licenses, many more based on only certain cars, drivers or events. <i><a href="/wiki/Sega_Rally" title="Sega Rally">Sega Rally</a></i> was released in 1995, <i><a href="/wiki/V-Rally" title="V-Rally">V-Rally</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_Rally" title="Top Gear Rally">Top Gear Rally</a></i> in 1997 and the first game in the very popular <i><a href="/wiki/Colin_McRae_Rally" title="Colin McRae Rally">Colin McRae Rally</a></i> series in 1998. <i><a href="/wiki/Rally_Trophy" title="Rally Trophy">Rally Trophy</a></i>, released in 2001 for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> by <a href="/wiki/Bugbear_Entertainment" title="Bugbear Entertainment">Bugbear</a>, concentrated on historic cars such as <a href="/wiki/Alpine_A110" title="Alpine A110">Alpine A110</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lancia_Stratos" title="Lancia Stratos">Lancia Stratos</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/RalliSport_Challenge" title="RalliSport Challenge">RalliSport Challenge</a></i>, released in 2002 for Windows and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_(console)" title="Xbox (console)">Xbox</a> by <a href="/wiki/Digital_Illusions_CE" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital Illusions CE">Digital Illusions CE</a>, featured classic <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> cars and <a href="/wiki/Hillclimbing" title="Hillclimbing">hillclimb</a> models along with modern WRC cars.\n</p><p>Fully FIA licensed <i><a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship_(video_game_series)" title="World Rally Championship (video game series)">WRC: World Rally Championship</a></i> was released in 2001 for <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> by <a href="/wiki/Evolution_Studios" title="Evolution Studios">Evolution Studios</a>. The video game series had its fifth game, <i><a href="/wiki/WRC:_Rally_Evolved" title="WRC: Rally Evolved">WRC: Rally Evolved</a></i>, in 2005. <a href="/wiki/Sim_racing" title="Sim racing">Racing simulator</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Richard_Burns_Rally" title="Richard Burns Rally">Richard Burns Rally</a></i>, released in 2004 for several platforms, has gathered recognition for its realism. Recent top-selling games include <i><a href="/wiki/Colin_McRae:_DiRT_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Colin McRae: DiRT 2">Colin McRae: DiRT 2</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sega_Rally_Revo" title="Sega Rally Revo">Sega Rally Revo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dirt_3" title="Dirt 3">Dirt 3</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Gran_Turismo_5" title="Gran Turismo 5">Gran Turismo 5</a></i> will include the WRC totally licensed. In October 2010, <a href="/wiki/Black_Bean_Games" title="Black Bean Games">Black Bean Games</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/WRC:_FIA_World_Rally_Championship_(2010_video_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="WRC: FIA World Rally Championship (2010 video game)">WRC: FIA World Rally Championship</a></i> which features the cars, drivers and events of the <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Rally_Championship" title="2010 World Rally Championship">2010 World Rally Championship</a>, including those from the three support categories. A downloadable patch was produced allowing players to drive in Group B cars such as the Audi Quattro.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  Various cars whose participated in the WRC such as <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Lancer_WRC" title="Mitsubishi Lancer WRC">Mitsubishi Lancer WRC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta_RS_WRC" title="Ford Fiesta RS WRC">Ford Fiesta RS WRC</a> have also appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> game <i><a href="/wiki/Car_Town" title="Car Town">Car Town</a></i>. The WRC video game license was acquired by French game development studio <a href="/wiki/Kylotonn" title="Kylotonn">Kylotonn</a> from <a href="/wiki/Milestone_S.r.l." title="Milestone S.r.l.">Milestone S.r.l.</a> after the release of <a href="/wiki/WRC_4:_FIA_World_Rally_Championship" title="WRC 4: FIA World Rally Championship">WRC 4: FIA World Rally Championship in 2013</a>. The first WRC game by Kylotonn was <a href="/wiki/WRC_5" title="WRC 5">WRC 5</a>, released in 2015. This was followed by <a href="/wiki/WRC_6" title="WRC 6">WRC 6</a> in 2016, and <a href="/wiki/WRC_7" title="WRC 7">WRC 7</a> in 2017.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_records" title="List of World Rally Championship records">List of World Rally Championship records</a></li></ul>\n<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Office-book.svg/30px-Office-book.svg.png" width="30" height="30" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Office-book.svg/45px-Office-book.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Office-book.svg/60px-Office-book.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><ul style="font-weight: bold">\n<li><a href="/wiki/Book:Rallying" title="Book:Rallying">Book: Rallying</a></li>\n</ul></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
